  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dfa20aed-2eb2-4969-a782-2745306505f4'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_25956934" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25956934" />
    <a title="Petra-X" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1237196-petra-x"><img alt="Petra-X" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603179398p2/1237196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/25956934?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petra-X" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petra-X" href="/user/show/1237196-petra-x">Petra-X</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780753810491" href="/book/show/251502.Under_Milk_Wood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=poetry-drama">poetry-drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25956934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3397155692036793242">Some works of literature just beg to be read out loud - This is the House that Jack Built and Hiawatha are two that most people are familiar with. Under Milk Wood too, is better appreciated read aloud. <br/><br/>Try it for yourself. A sample (read aloud with Welsh accent, sing-song, go up like a question at the end of the line, extend vowels, as in 'weeedkiller' and emphasis is usually on the first syllable.)<br/><br/>FIRST VOICE<br/><br/>Mr Pugh, in the School House opposite, takes up the morning<br/>tea to Mrs Pugh, and whisper</span>
  <span id="freeText3397155692036793242" style="display:none">Some works of literature just beg to be read out loud - This is the House that Jack Built and Hiawatha are two that most people are familiar with. Under Milk Wood too, is better appreciated read aloud. <br /><br />Try it for yourself. A sample (read aloud with Welsh accent, sing-song, go up like a question at the end of the line, extend vowels, as in 'weeedkiller' and emphasis is usually on the first syllable.)<br /><br />FIRST VOICE<br /><br />Mr Pugh, in the School House opposite, takes up the morning<br />tea to Mrs Pugh, and whispers on the stairs<br /><br /> MR. PUGH<br /><br />Here's your arsenic, dear.<br />And your weedkiller biscuit.<br />I've throttled your parakeet.<br />I've spat in the vases.<br />I've put cheese in the mouseholes.<br />Here's your... [_Door creaks open_<br /> ...nice tea, dear.<br /><br /> MRS PUGH<br /><br />Too much sugar.<br /><br />Or try this, read by Richard Burton, who was also from the same area so has exactly the right intonation. <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=WJtzOD3KbLM" rel="nofollow noopener">full cast production of Under Milk Wood</a> If you would like to listen to a young Richard Burton reading the play alone (which I much prefer), it is in two parts, <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gymiPlOqsY0" rel="nofollow noopener">part one</a> and <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cWqHP9l8EKo" rel="nofollow noopener">part two</a>.<br /><br />When I read this play by Dylan Thomas, I hear the village life of my childhood come to life. He caught the lilt and cadence of the Valleys speech and the trivial preoccupations of the people perfectly. Of course it helps that like Dylan Thomas I am also from South Wales and have the accent down pat!<br /><br />A little known fact, apparent to all Welsh people but no-one else, is that the village of Llareggub which looks perfectly Welsh is actually the English Bugger All backwards. (If it had been Welsh it would have been Llanreggub and mean the Parish of St. Reggub).<br /><br />Dylan Thomas wasn't at all poetic, his poems are just as much for people who don't like poetry as those who like reading it and contemplating what the poet meant by his imagery. There is not such issue with Dylan Thomas, he says what he means and you get it straightaway. <br /><br />If you enjoyed the play, read Dylan Thomas's magnificent [book:Do Not Go Gentle Into That Good Night|6619539]. <br /><br /><i>Considerably rewritten 18 October on being told the link to Under Milk Wood no longer worked.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3397155692036793242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/860282741" />
    <a title="s.penkevich" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6431467-s-penkevich"><img alt="s.penkevich" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587089836p2/6431467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/860282741?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="s.penkevich" class="user" itemprop="url" name="s.penkevich" href="/user/show/6431467-s-penkevich">s.penkevich</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">The lovers, the dreamers, and me</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to s.penkevich by: </span>
      Lauren
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431467-s-penkevich?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431467-s-penkevich?shelf=plays">plays</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431467-s-penkevich?shelf=dreamlike">dreamlike</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer860282741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9896798900894924190"><i>We are not wholly bad or good, who live our lives under Milk Wood.</i><br/><br/>The voices of Dylan Thomas’ <i>Under Milk Wood</i> rise and fall, crashing into each other like waves under a milky moon, their sweet prose an effervescence of sounds and syllables to intoxicate the soul. This ‘play for voices’ follows the lives of the citizens of Milk Wood across a full day, bookmarked by the surrealistically sensational dream sequences of the two nights. The play simply engulfs you in its beautiful embrace, like the wa</span>
  <span id="freeText9896798900894924190" style="display:none"><i>We are not wholly bad or good, who live our lives under Milk Wood.</i><br /><br />The voices of Dylan Thomas’ <i>Under Milk Wood</i> rise and fall, crashing into each other like waves under a milky moon, their sweet prose an effervescence of sounds and syllables to intoxicate the soul. This ‘play for voices’ follows the lives of the citizens of Milk Wood across a full day, bookmarked by the surrealistically sensational dream sequences of the two nights. The play simply engulfs you in its beautiful embrace, like the warm encompassing feeling of sleep overtaking you under the coziest of blankets with the redolence of summer majesty breezing through an open window. <i>Under Milk Wood</i> offers a unique voyeuristic vantage-point for the reader—or listener—as they see all the hopes and dreams swimming in the hearts of these simple folks and watch them interact with one another. From dark and somber to hilarious and cynical, the spectrum of emotions and existence swings and sways to the vocal rhythm of Thomas’ sharp pen and wit. There is the aging sea captain haunted in dreams by pallid corpses speaking from their watery grave, the wife intent on poisoning her husband, the innocent cruelty of children, the lust of the village strumpet and the condescending remarks of those around her; all walks of life exist in the boundaries of this quiet village that could be any village. It satisfied my thirst for something similar to Woolf’s masterpiece <i>The Waves</i> and filled me with joy during the brief sitting it takes to read this play. Charged by the power of Thomas’ prose, sharpened over a distinguished career as a masterful poet, and alive with the madness and love of life, this ‘play for voices’ is an entertaining and exquisite event to read or listen to. <br /><b>4.5/5</b><br /><br /><i>The only sea I saw<br />Was the seesaw sea<br />With you riding on it.<br />Lie down, lie easy.<br />Let me shipwreck in your thighs.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9896798900894924190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18224086" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18224086" />
    <a title="Trevor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/175635-trevor"><img alt="Trevor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565151545p2/175635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18224086?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trevor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trevor" href="/user/show/175635-trevor">Trevor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/175635-trevor?shelf=literature">literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18224086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4831980228886176458">I can honestly say that the world would be a lesser place if I had never read this play. It is not just that it is laugh-out-loud funny or that it is sad enough to make me weep - Captain Cat being forgotten by Rosie near the end is almost too painful to remember. But it is so full, so wonderfully overflowing with all the day to day concerns of life and love that it is a world in and of itself. Here is true creative genius.<br/><br/>From husbands purchasing books on how to poison their wives to the terribl</span>
  <span id="freeText4831980228886176458" style="display:none">I can honestly say that the world would be a lesser place if I had never read this play. It is not just that it is laugh-out-loud funny or that it is sad enough to make me weep - Captain Cat being forgotten by Rosie near the end is almost too painful to remember. But it is so full, so wonderfully overflowing with all the day to day concerns of life and love that it is a world in and of itself. Here is true creative genius.<br /><br />From husbands purchasing books on how to poison their wives to the terrible things we dream in the silence of the night, to postmen's wives steaming open mail and then their mailman husbands telling everyone what is in their letters. Listen. You can hear their voices speaking to you across the darkness and over the soft hush of the waves lapping at the shore while gently raising the boats of the fishermen who are drinking at the bar all day long because it is always just after opening time. You can sing along to the bawdy songs of the drunks or listen with blind Captain Cat as he identifies people in their passing by the tap of their steps on the cobbles or the sudden silence of the women pretending not to notice Polly who the police are sure to come after sooner or later. You can dream with the Sea Captain as the faces of the long dead come out of the sea to greet him each in their turn. Or if you are quiet, you can share in the lustful desires of a young girl tucked up toasty in her bed with her hairy lover rudely wagging his tail or lie starched in the icy cold sheets of a widow who remains anything but snug though forever bookended between her two dead husbands.<br /><br />The children's songs will dance in your mind for years - I bought the George Martin production of this play when the kids were born and have sung them Johnny Crack and Flossy Snail ever since - even now they are both in their late teens.<br /><br />There are 'adult themes' in this book, and not just because one of the characters is a loose woman with quite a few too many babies - but everyone has either two wives or two husbands or too few husbands or a wife too many. <br /><br />The characters just stay with you - butchers selling man chop and bakers' wives who have to borrow loaves of bread from neighbours because the baker forgot the bread, wives who have two husbands, a sober and a drunk one, and my favourite, No Good Boyo, up to no good and who has the best line in the whole play - one I repeatedly quote at random when odd things happen in my life and which, if I'm overheard, no one ever seems to understand - "Bloody funny fish."<br /><br />But the language, the song of the words, the lilt and crackle and exuberance of words themselves at play - god, to be able to write like that. Okay, so he was a poet, but with such an ear. And an eye for life and a hand that could balance the worth of a line and not give it either too much weight or too little, but just enough.<br /><br />Time passes, listen, time passes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4831980228886176458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2976979972" />
    <a title="Kimber Silver" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92166434-kimber-silver"><img alt="Kimber Silver" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547493035p2/92166434.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2976979972?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimber Silver" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimber Silver" href="/user/show/92166434-kimber-silver">Kimber Silver</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92166434-kimber-silver?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92166434-kimber-silver?shelf=epic-reads">epic-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92166434-kimber-silver?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92166434-kimber-silver?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92166434-kimber-silver?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92166434-kimber-silver?shelf=delicious-writing">delicious-writing</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2976979972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8640179752501041531">Originally written for BBC radio, the rise and fall of the voices are like the slow roll of the ocean. After reading it, I wished that I had opted for the audiobook. <i>Under Milk Wood</i> would be spectacular when read aloud.<br/><br/>The setting is a Welsh fishing village just tucking in for the night. From the first line, the dreamy lyrical prose captured my imagination, painting a clear picture of the locale and its residents.<br/><br/><i>"To begin at the beginning:<br/>It is Spring, moonless night in the small town, starless</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8640179752501041531" style="display:none">Originally written for BBC radio, the rise and fall of the voices are like the slow roll of the ocean. After reading it, I wished that I had opted for the audiobook. <i>Under Milk Wood</i> would be spectacular when read aloud.<br /><br />The setting is a Welsh fishing village just tucking in for the night. From the first line, the dreamy lyrical prose captured my imagination, painting a clear picture of the locale and its residents.<br /><br /><i>"To begin at the beginning:<br />It is Spring, moonless night in the small town, starless and bible-black, the cobblestreets silent and the hunched, courters’-and-rabbits’ wood limping invisible down to the sloeblack, slow, black, crowblack, fishingboat-bobbing sea."</i><br /><br />As I strolled through the sleeping town of Llareggub, I caught snippets of the things dreams are made of-from candy to crinoline and loving to laughable. I was drawn into each dreamer’s secret world by night and their curious routines by day.<br /><br />This play strikes all the right notes with laughter, heartache and even some naughty bits! <i>Under Milk Wood</i> is an engaging read.<br /><br /><i>"You can hear the dew falling, and the hushed town breathing."</i><br /><br /><i>"Time passes. Listen. Time passes.<br />Come closer now.<br />Only you can hear the houses sleeping in the streets in the slow deep salt and the silent black, bandaged night."</i></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2444219468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9078314864608933400">Thomas's voices are like a tide that's rising and falling in spite of the reader's convenience at the time of the reading. Like a choir of ghosts ignorant of their unsubstantial nature. I swear they gave me the chills a number of times while I was reading it during my night shift, not because it was particularly scary but because of the everyday humour and grief that they were drenched in. Such darkness, such humour, such insolent irony in such a haunting combination I've rarely come across, if </span>
  <span id="freeText9078314864608933400" style="display:none">Thomas's voices are like a tide that's rising and falling in spite of the reader's convenience at the time of the reading. Like a choir of ghosts ignorant of their unsubstantial nature. I swear they gave me the chills a number of times while I was reading it during my night shift, not because it was particularly scary but because of the everyday humour and grief that they were drenched in. Such darkness, such humour, such insolent irony in such a haunting combination I've rarely come across, if ever, in my time as a reader. I curse my fate for not being Welsh, for if I were, I'm sure, the sentiments would be far more intense.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18402506029684932544"><i>"This town's as full as a lovebird's egg."</i><br/>- Dylan Thomas, Under Milk Wood<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488610173i/22135574._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='488' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book has languished on my shelf.<br/>Ignored.<br/>Left alone. <br/><br/>I bought this book years ago. It was a deal. It was a steal. It was $2 at Goodwill. I recognized Dylan Thomas and knew it was a Folio edition. $2? Value? Done. I brought it home, put it on the shelf. Thought about it only narrowly. I figured it was a book of poetry. Poems. Fights against the dying of the light and whatnots. <br/><br/>Nope. It is certainly poetic. Lyrical. Whims</span>
  <span id="freeText18402506029684932544" style="display:none"><i>"This town's as full as a lovebird's egg."</i><br>- Dylan Thomas, Under Milk Wood<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488610173i/22135574._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="488" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book has languished on my shelf.<br>Ignored.<br>Left alone. <br><br>I bought this book years ago. It was a deal. It was a steal. It was $2 at Goodwill. I recognized Dylan Thomas and knew it was a Folio edition. $2? Value? Done. I brought it home, put it on the shelf. Thought about it only narrowly. I figured it was a book of poetry. Poems. Fights against the dying of the light and whatnots. <br><br>Nope. It is certainly poetic. Lyrical. Whimsical. A play, however. Meant for many voices. An innovation for Radio. Meant to be read. Think of later James Joyce, but something easy to understand. A well-spoken lust dream in a Welch coastal town.<br><br>So, ignored on the shelf? Why now? I'm trying and dying to read 100 books, during the first 100 days of either the year (closer) or year + Trump's 100 days (more than 100 I guess). So on days when I don't have 4+ hours to read, or the book I want to read is bigger than 240 pages, I generally use small books of poetry or philosophy to bridge a larger book into smaller bites without violating my first rule (1 book a day). So, yes, I am anal retentive about even things I enjoy. <br><br>So, back to Under Milk Wood. If you have the opportunity to read it, read it. If you have the opportunity to listen to either Dylan Thomas &amp; Co read it, listen. Richard Burton &amp; Co is also a nice treat.<br><br>Some of my favorite lines:<br><br>"It is spring, moonless night in the small town, starless and bible-black, the cobble streets silent and the hunched, courters'-and-blackrabbits' wood limping invisible down to the shoeblack, slow, black, crowblack, fishingboat-bobbing sea."<br><br><i>"From where you are you can hear their dreams."</i><br><br><i>"And before you let the sun in, mind it wipes its shoes."</i><br><br><i>"And high above, in Salt Lake Farm, Mr Utah Watkins counts, all night, the wife-faced sheep as they leap the fences on the hill, smiling and knitting and bleating just like Mrs. Utah Watkins."</i><br><br>"...who kissed her once by the pig-sty when she wasn't looking and never kissed her again although she was looking all the time."<br><br><i>"Time Passes. Listen. Time passes. An owl flies home past Bethesda, to a chapel in an oak. And the dawn inches up."</i><br><br><i>"There is no leg belonging to the foot that belongs to this shoe."</i></span>

<div id="review_238088523" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238088523" />
    <a title="Shovelmonkey1" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3926982-shovelmonkey1"><img alt="Shovelmonkey1" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391713268p2/3926982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238088523?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shovelmonkey1" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shovelmonkey1" href="/user/show/3926982-shovelmonkey1">Shovelmonkey1</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238088523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12694363461122190819">I like Dylan Thomas for two reasons<br/>1. I grew up in Wales <br/>2. I read his book Under Milk Wood when I was in school.<br/><br/>Wales is a strange place to grow up. For a start you're told as a child that it's full of castles and dragons and daffodils and that there is evil over the border (England) and that Rugby is the one true sport. Some of those things are true. I'm sure even Dylan Thomas thought them from time to time. I lived outside Cardiff and Thomas was busily engaged in being Welsh in and around the</span>
  <span id="freeText12694363461122190819" style="display:none">I like Dylan Thomas for two reasons<br />1. I grew up in Wales <br />2. I read his book Under Milk Wood when I was in school.<br /><br />Wales is a strange place to grow up. For a start you're told as a child that it's full of castles and dragons and daffodils and that there is evil over the border (England) and that Rugby is the one true sport. Some of those things are true. I'm sure even Dylan Thomas thought them from time to time. I lived outside Cardiff and Thomas was busily engaged in being Welsh in and around the area of Swansea which is just a bit further along the coast. He described Swansea as an "ugly lovely town" which was then translated in the film Twin Towns to " a pretty shitty city". A bit unfair perhaps but then Swansea is fairly unlovely. The area of the Mumbles however is stunning and its natural beauty which influenced Thomas, should not be overlooked.<br /><br />Reading Under Milk Wood was simultaneously fun and a form of torture for me as we read it out loud and tried in turn to make it replicate the radio play it was originally supposed to be. The characters of Llareggub were supposed to spring to life in our hands and through our voices. I can still remember chunks of the text "Nothing grows in my garden, only washing and babies", springs to mind first and foremost. As a child this made me ponder about what sort of green fingeredness it would take for children to start sprouting in the back yard. <br /><br />Unfortunately as I'd only recently arrived from Edinburgh, where I was initially educated, my "valleys" accent left a little to be desired. Everyone else already had a welsh accent and could just lay it on a bit more thickly to create a passable approximation of a valley twang and then there was me with a Scots brogue trying to sound like one of the Mrs Dai Breads for the recording we were making and failing miserably. <br /><br />Part send up, part caricature, part hymn to the eccentricities of a welsh town Under Milk Wood is post war Wales at its colourful best.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12694363461122190819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1127401335" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1127401335" />
    <a title="Mimi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2490110-mimi"><img alt="Mimi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424631975p2/2490110.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1127401335?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi" href="/user/show/2490110-mimi">Mimi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140188882" href="/book/show/251504.Under_Milk_Wood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1127401335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11906907387524783798">Not a play or a poem, exactly. This was written to be performed as a BBC radio drama, and it's about life in a sleepy town in Wales. We follow a few characters as they go from dream to wakefulness and then move through the rest of their day. We get to hear their thoughts and reflections as they do every day things. Sounds very dull, I know, which is why you have to read (or listen to) it for yourself.<br/><br/>In the tradition of small towns (both fictional and nonfictional), everyone has a big secret. Ea</span>
  <span id="freeText11906907387524783798" style="display:none">Not a play or a poem, exactly. This was written to be performed as a BBC radio drama, and it's about life in a sleepy town in Wales. We follow a few characters as they go from dream to wakefulness and then move through the rest of their day. We get to hear their thoughts and reflections as they do every day things. Sounds very dull, I know, which is why you have to read (or listen to) it for yourself.<br /><br />In the tradition of small towns (both fictional and nonfictional), everyone has a big secret. Each character is haunted by old ghosts and rivals, and all are hiding their true intentions, and at least one has murder on the mind. Not so dull once you go further into the story. The writing is incredibly interesting in its simplicity and depth. Dylan Thomas has a thing for lyrical wordplay, and his prose can speak volumes in just a couple of lines.<br /><br />What's most fascinating to me about this piece is the way it reads like a slightly discomforting tour guide of this seemingly quaint little town. You get to take a walk about the town and see the sights, but beyond that, you also get to see into the people who live there. And these people sort of hate each other, but they're sort of stuck to the town. So a lot of forced niceties are exchanged on the surface, but behind the smiles and small talks, they're imagining each other dead.<br /><br /><br />Originally posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://covers2covers.wordpress.com/2014/12/13/1562/">https://covers2covers.wordpress.com/2...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11906907387524783798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_538349712" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/538349712" />
    <a title="Warwick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53165-warwick"><img alt="Warwick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510406793p2/53165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/538349712?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warwick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warwick" href="/user/show/53165-warwick">Warwick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/12402469-under-milk-wood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53165-warwick?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53165-warwick?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53165-warwick?shelf=folio-society">folio-society</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53165-warwick?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53165-warwick?shelf=wales">wales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer538349712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17381428200907212428">A smorgasbord of language. I am still blown away every time I read that first measured sentence, about the woodland ‘limping invisible down to the sloeblack, slow, black, crowblack, fishingboat-bobbing sea’.<br/><br/>If you only knew Dylan Thomas from his short poems (as I did before I read this) then prepare for a very pleasant shock. The wonderful rhythm of the lines here, the extraordinary creativity of compound words and unexpected similes, all sustained over a considerable distance, is something quit</span>
  <span id="freeText17381428200907212428" style="display:none">A smorgasbord of language. I am still blown away every time I read that first measured sentence, about the woodland ‘limping invisible down to the sloeblack, slow, black, crowblack, fishingboat-bobbing sea’.<br /><br />If you only knew Dylan Thomas from his short poems (as I did before I read this) then prepare for a very pleasant shock. The wonderful rhythm of the lines here, the extraordinary creativity of compound words and unexpected similes, all sustained over a considerable distance, is something quite distinctive and entirely absorbing. And surprisingly funny at times: there is a lot of warm, affectionate interplay between the different characters of this sleepy Welsh town, rivalries, fantasies, frustrations, sexual liaisons real and imagined, boredom, dreams – everything you'd expect from small-town life is here.<br /><br />But it's the poetic language that makes me really love it. The ‘sunhoneyed cobbles’, the ‘dumb goose-hiss of the wives’, Gossamer Benyon who is ‘spoonstirred and quivering’ and who ‘high-heels out of school’ – milk churns that stand ‘like short, silver policemen’, and lovers in ‘the grassgreen gooseberried double bed of the wood’ – it's all described as though in the throes of some ecstatic vision, which I suppose is what good poetry should be like.<br /><br />I don't want to overstate my case <i>too</i> much, but go <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=uuPO2Kvqlms" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> and listen to Richard Burton reading the opening section, and if you're not rolling on the floor in delight after about thirty seconds, then you probably have no soul.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17381428200907212428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4826985187799684567">Drama, poetry or comedy?, how about all of them. Centering around one day in a small, unexceptional Welsh coastal town. We first meet those who recide at a point before dawn, the night "flying like black flour", as the reader drifts off through the dark fields and streets, through the bedrooms of the sleeping residents and into their dreams. From there we watch as they wake up and work, following them out of bed over this one day and then finally back into bed as night falls.<br/><br/>The melodic and beau</span>
  <span id="freeText4826985187799684567" style="display:none">Drama, poetry or comedy?, how about all of them. Centering around one day in a small, unexceptional Welsh coastal town. We first meet those who recide at a point before dawn, the night "flying like black flour", as the reader drifts off through the dark fields and streets, through the bedrooms of the sleeping residents and into their dreams. From there we watch as they wake up and work, following them out of bed over this one day and then finally back into bed as night falls.<br /><br />The melodic and beautiful use of language creates a charming world, through a lens we affectionately observe all their passions, predicaments, comings and goings. He writes with great warmth, rogues and saints alike treated with charity and humour. Thomas views all characters with an easy sympathy, happy to be in their company. A spirited toast to humanity, he makes the sun shine in the most dullest of places. Along with Daffodils, leeks and sheep, Thomas is another with a strong symbolic meaning.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4826985187799684567" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText3273465286438774627" style="display:none">“Sundown dazzling day gold through my eyes but my eyes turned within only see starless and bible black…” <b>King Crimson</b> – <i>Starless</i>.<br /><i>Under Milk Wood</i> has a texture of a lyrical myth so it is timeless…<br />People sleep and they dream... People wake up and they play fools, dawdle, muck around, misbehave, recollect, fantasize and build castles in the air…<br />“There's the clip clop of horses on the sun-honeyed cobbles of the humming streets, hammering of horse-shoes, gobble quack and cackle, tomtit twitter from the bird-ounced boughs, braying on Donkey Down. Bread is baking, pigs are grunting, chop goes the butcher, milk-churns bell, tills ring, sheep cough, dogs shout, saws sing. Oh, the Spring whinny and morning moo from the clog dancing farms, the gulls’ gab and rabble on the boat-bobbing river and sea and the cockles bubbling in the sand, scamper of sanderlings, curlew cry, crow caw, pigeon coo, clock strike, bull bellow, and the ragged gabble of the bear garden school as the women scratch and babble in Mrs Organ Morgan's general shop where everything is sold: custard, buckets, henna, rat-traps, shrimp-nets, sugar, stamps, confetti, paraffin, hatchets, whistles.”<br />People love and hate… People live.<br />“Bible black and captain cat keeps the world inside his hat with deep dry wells and cockled shells he holds his wife beneath his paws…” <b>The Coral</b> – <i>Milkwood Blues</i>.</span>

<div id="review_362932621" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362932621" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4542979-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454402751p2/4542979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/362932621?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/4542979-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=plays-seen">plays-seen</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362932621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1564254135144428474"><br/>Dylan Thomas originally intended this work to be radio play. However, my first experience of it was seeing the film adaptation narrated by Richard Burton, back when I was in high school in the 1970s. I remember two things about the experience: loving the sound of Richard Burton's voice, and feeling overwhelmed. This extract from the <a href='http://movies.nytimes.com/movie/review?res=9401E2DC1531EF34BC4A51DFB7668388669EDE' rel='nofollow noopener'>review in the New York Times</a> goes some way to explaining my reaction: <br/><blockquote>Too many words, perhaps, for the stage. Too many words, I'm convinced, for the screen. It's not</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1564254135144428474" style="display:none"><br />Dylan Thomas originally intended this work to be radio play. However, my first experience of it was seeing the film adaptation narrated by Richard Burton, back when I was in high school in the 1970s. I remember two things about the experience: loving the sound of Richard Burton's voice, and feeling overwhelmed. This extract from the <a href="http://movies.nytimes.com/movie/review?res=9401E2DC1531EF34BC4A51DFB7668388669EDE" rel="nofollow noopener">review in the New York Times</a> goes some way to explaining my reaction: <br /><blockquote>Too many words, perhaps, for the stage. Too many words, I'm convinced, for the screen. It's not simply the quantity of words, though. It's also their ornateness. They overflow the ears and get into the eyes. Great clouds of them everywhere, like swarms of big soft gnats. They won't stop, and they make the job of the film adapter almost impossible.</blockquote><br />Since then I've read the play and seen at least one stage production. However, it took until today, when I saw <a href="http://blogs.crikey.com.au/curtaincall/2012/05/29/review-under-milk-wood-drama-theatre-sydney/" rel="nofollow noopener">this production</a> by the Sydney Theatre Company that I came to fully appreciate not just the magic of Thomas' words, but the fact that a stage production really can work. The production was wonderful and the words are still racing around inside my head. <br /><br />A few years ago, my daughter recited these lines from the play at the wedding of her best friend to a Welsh boy. This is what Mr Edwards says to Miss Price:<br /><blockquote>I am a draper mad with love. I love you more than all the flannelette and calico, candlewick, dimity, crash and merino, tussore, cretonne, crepon, muslin, poplin, ticking and twill in the whole Cloth Hall of the world. I have come to take you away to my Emporium on the hill, where the change hums on wires. Throw away your little bedsocks and your Welsh wool knitted jacket, I will warm the sheets like an electric toaster, I will lie by your side like the Sunday roast.</blockquote><br />Wonderful, wonderful writing. The great clouds of words no longer overwhelm me. They transport me.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1564254135144428474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_882109983" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/882109983" />
    <a title="Fiona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7232207-fiona"><img alt="Fiona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472071438p2/7232207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/882109983?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fiona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fiona" href="/user/show/7232207-fiona">Fiona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780753810491" href="/book/show/251502.Under_Milk_Wood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7232207-fiona?shelf=i-taught-this-book">i-taught-this-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer882109983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2037016852125471510">I remember the first time I came across <i>Under Milk Wood</i>, and it was when I was learning about imagery for my GCSEs. I fell in love with it - and, of course, with Richard Burton's beautiful First Voice.<br/><br/>One joy of being an English teacher is teaching your favourite texts to someone new - which I'm pretty sure was what was happening to to me, the first time I was taught this. It wasn't on the syllabus.<br/><br/>Another joy is that you can take playful, inventive, poetic language and give it to a kid who's in</span>
  <span id="freeText2037016852125471510" style="display:none">I remember the first time I came across <i>Under Milk Wood</i>, and it was when I was learning about imagery for my GCSEs. I fell in love with it - and, of course, with Richard Burton's beautiful First Voice.<br /><br />One joy of being an English teacher is teaching your favourite texts to someone new - which I'm pretty sure was what was happening to to me, the first time I was taught this. It wasn't on the syllabus.<br /><br />Another joy is that you can take playful, inventive, poetic language and give it to a kid who's inevitably petrified by it. And then you can break it down, and explain it to them, and it's a bit like you're showing someone a secret language, a second story just underneath the surface of the one you're reading, and you can watch that kid go from fear and mistrust, to real appreciation of rhythm and metaphor and description and sound - right in front of your eyes. It's like magic. I'll never get tired of it as long as I live.<br /><br />We spent an hour and a half on the opening monologue, and then the same again comparing it with the use of pace, sound, description of night time in Auden's <a href="http://www.allanyeo.co.uk/html/the_night_mail.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Night Mail</a>. I got to remember exactly what I love about linguistic gymnastics, and as for him, he'll never be scared of poetry, or imagery, again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2037016852125471510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_401628999" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/401628999" />
    <a title="P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3135769-p"><img alt="P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430648532p2/3135769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/401628999?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="P." href="/user/show/3135769-p">P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3135769-p?shelf=plays">plays</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3135769-p?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3135769-p?shelf=booksread2012">booksread2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer401628999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14825884911251731550">OK, I don't know what this is, but it's not your average play... Under Milk Wood is something else. It deserves its own category. Shortly before his death I reckon Dylan Thomas came sublimely close to the perfect narrative. Readers of 'Cold Comfort Farm' will definitely recognise an Aunt Ada Doom-ish humour that rides on the coattails of stream of consciousness. <br/><br/>Under Milk Wood is very hard to pin down as it's a mix of so many things, and that's what makes it so astonishingly brilliant. It delve</span>
  <span id="freeText14825884911251731550" style="display:none">OK, I don't know what this is, but it's not your average play... Under Milk Wood is something else. It deserves its own category. Shortly before his death I reckon Dylan Thomas came sublimely close to the perfect narrative. Readers of 'Cold Comfort Farm' will definitely recognise an Aunt Ada Doom-ish humour that rides on the coattails of stream of consciousness. <br /><br />Under Milk Wood is very hard to pin down as it's a mix of so many things, and that's what makes it so astonishingly brilliant. It delves into the unlikely dreams and nightmares of a small Welsh port town (quite literally), which shocking hinge rather a lot on sex, love, longing and even murder. Let's put it this way, their waking dreams do not waver much from their night ones! Having said that, it is rather hilarious and had me in stitches at one point. Who said that inbred villagers were boring? Every character is a fascination unto itself; paragons of the town gossip and the village idiot head a wonderfully rich cast which is further enriched by a dynamic, odd yet strangely 'on the ball' type of language. In fact if words could be tasted and felt like tangible things, then the only place you could experience that would be in Under Milk Wood. <br /><br />You must read it and see for yourself.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14825884911251731550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1779738249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1779738249" />
    <a title="Bam cooks the books ;-)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5922426-bam-cooks-the-books--"><img alt="Bam cooks the books ;-)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559653145p2/5922426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1779738249?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bam cooks the books ;-)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bam cooks the books ;-)" href="/user/show/5922426-bam-cooks-the-books--">Bam cooks the books ;-)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5922426-bam-cooks-the-books--?shelf=plays">plays</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5922426-bam-cooks-the-books--?shelf=2016-reading-challenge">2016-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1779738249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10097591999128549774">Here we enter the lives of the residents of Milk Wood, a Welsh seaside town, first through their dreams, then through their daytime interactions with each other. As in all of our lives, some moments are terribly laugh-out-loud funny, some poignantly sad. Dylan Thomas was quite the wordsmith! Sub-titled "A Play for Voices," I would love to hear voices perform this play someday. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer14558750463567330138"><b>Hate</b>:<br/><br/>MRS PUGH<br/><br/>Give me the parcel.<br/><br/> WILLY NILLY [postman whose wife reads all the mail to him before he delivers it:]<br/><br/>It's for Mr Pugh, Mrs Pugh.<br/><br/> MRS PUGH<br/><br/>Never you mind. What's inside it?<br/><br/> WILLY NILLY<br/><br/>A book called Lives of the Great Poisoners.<br/><br/>[later:]<br/><br/>MRS PUGH<br/><br/>Persons with manners do not read at table,<br/><br/> FIRST VOICE<br/><br/>says Mrs Pugh. She swallows a digestive tablet as big as a<br/>horse-pill, washing it down with clouded peasoup water.<br/><br/> [Pause:]<br/><br/> MRS PUGH<br/><br/>Some persons were brought up in pigsties.<br/><br/> MR PUGH<br/><br/>Pigs don't r</span>
  <span id="freeText14558750463567330138" style="display:none"><b>Hate</b>:<br /><br />MRS PUGH<br /><br />Give me the parcel.<br /><br /> WILLY NILLY [postman whose wife reads all the mail to him before he delivers it:]<br /><br />It's for Mr Pugh, Mrs Pugh.<br /><br /> MRS PUGH<br /><br />Never you mind. What's inside it?<br /><br /> WILLY NILLY<br /><br />A book called Lives of the Great Poisoners.<br /><br />[later:]<br /><br />MRS PUGH<br /><br />Persons with manners do not read at table,<br /><br /> FIRST VOICE<br /><br />says Mrs Pugh. She swallows a digestive tablet as big as a<br />horse-pill, washing it down with clouded peasoup water.<br /><br /> [Pause:]<br /><br /> MRS PUGH<br /><br />Some persons were brought up in pigsties.<br /><br /> MR PUGH<br /><br />Pigs don't read at table, dear.<br /><br /> FIRST VOICE<br /><br />Bitterly she flicks dust from the broken cruet. It settles<br />on the pie in a thin gnat-rain.<br /><br /> MR PUGH<br /><br />Pigs can't read, my dear.<br /><br /> MRS PUGH<br /><br />I know one who can.<br /><br /> FIRST VOICE<br /><br />Alone in the hissing laboratory of his wishes, Mr Pugh<br />minces among bad vats and jeroboams, tiptoes through<br />spinneys of murdering herbs, agony dancing in his<br />crucibles, and mixes especially for Mrs Pugh a venomous<br />porridge unknown to toxicologists which will scald and<br />viper through her until her ears fall off like figs, her<br />toes grow big and black as balloons, and steam comes<br />screaming out of her navel.<br /><br /> MR PUGH<br /><br />You know best, dear,<br /><br /> FIRST VOICE<br /><br />says Mr Pugh, and quick as a flash he ducks her in rat<br />soup.<br /><br /> MRS PUGH<br /><br />What's that book by your trough, Mr Pugh?<br /><br /> MR PUGH<br /><br />It's a theological work, my dear. Lives of the Great<br />Saints.<br /><br /> FIRST VOICE<br /><br />Mrs Pugh smiles. An icicle forms in the cold air of the<br />dining-vault.<br /><br />[later:]<br /><br />MRS PUGH<br /><br />Persons with manners,<br /><br /> SECOND VOICE<br /><br />snaps Mrs cold Pugh,<br /><br /> MRS PUGH<br /><br />do not nod at table.<br /><br /> FIRST VOICE<br /><br />Mr Pugh cringes awake. He puts on a soft-soaping smile: it<br />is sad and grey under his nicotine-eggyellow weeping<br />walrus Victorian moustache worn thick and long in memory<br />of Doctor Crippen.<br /><br /> MRS PUGH<br /><br />You should wait until you retire to your sty,<br /><br /> SECOND VOICE<br /><br />says Mrs Pugh, sweet as a razor. His fawning measly<br />quarter-smile freezes. Sly and silent, he foxes into his<br />chemist's den and there, in a hiss and prussic circle<br />of cauldrons and phials brimful with pox and the Black<br />Death, cooks up a fricassee of deadly nightshade,<br />nicotine, hot frog, cyanide and bat-spit for his needling<br />stalactite hag and bednag of a pokerbacked nutcracker<br />wife.<br /><br /> MR PUGH<br /><br />I beg your pardon, my dear,<br /><br /> SECOND VOICE<br /><br />he murmurs with a wheedle.<br /><br /><br /><b>Love</b>:<br /><br />FIRST VOICE<br /><br />Captain Cat, at his window thrown wide to the sun and the<br />clippered seas he sailed long ago when his eyes were blue<br />and bright, slumbers and voyages; ear-ringed and rolling,<br />I Love You Rosie Probert tattooed on his belly, he brawls<br />with broken bottles in the fug and babel of the dark dock<br />bars, roves with a herd of short and good time cows in<br />every naughty port and twines and souses with the drowned<br />and blowzy-breasted dead. He weeps as he sleeps and sails.<br /><br /> SECOND VOICE<br /><br />One voice of all he remembers most dearly as his dream<br />buckets down. Lazy early Rosie with the flaxen thatch,<br />whom he shared with Tom-Fred the donkeyman and many<br />another seaman, clearly and near to him speaks from the<br />bedroom of her dust. In that gulf and haven, fleets by the<br />dozen have anchored for the little heaven of the night;<br />but she speaks to Captain napping Cat alone. Mrs Probert...<br /><br /> ROSIE PROBERT<br /><br />from Duck Lane, Jack. Quack twice and ask for Rosie<br /><br /> SECOND VOICE<br /><br />...is the one love of his sea-life that was sardined with<br />women.<br /><br /> ROSIE PROBERT (Softly)<br /><br />What seas did you see,<br />Tom Cat, Tom Cat,<br />In your sailoring days<br />Long long ago?<br />What sea beasts were<br />In the wavery green<br />When you were my master?<br /><br /> CAPTAIN CAT<br /><br />I'll tell you the truth.<br />Seas barking like<br />seals, Blue seas and green,<br />Seas covered with eels<br />And mermen and whales.<br /><br /> ROSIE PROBERT<br /><br />What seas did you sail<br />Old whaler when<br />On the blubbery waves<br />Between Frisco and Wales<br />You were my bosun?<br /><br /> CAPTAIN CAT<br /><br />As true as I'm here<br />Dear you Tom Cat's tart<br />You landlubber Rosie<br />You cosy love<br />My easy as easy<br />My true sweetheart,<br />Seas green as a bean<br />Seas gliding with swans<br />In the seal-barking moon.<br /><br /> ROSIE PROBERT<br /><br />What seas were rocking<br />My little deck hand<br />My favourite husband <br />In your seaboots and hunger<br />My duck my whaler<br />My honey my daddy<br />My pretty sugar sailor.<br />With my name on your belly<br />When you were a boy<br />Long long ago?<br /><br /> CAPTAIN CAT<br /><br />I'll tell you no lies.<br />The only sea I saw<br />Was the seesaw sea<br />With you riding on it.<br />Lie down, lie easy.<br />Let me shipwreck in your thighs.<br /><br /> ROSIE PROBERT,<br /><br />Knock twice, Jack,<br />At the door of my grave<br />And ask for Rosie.<br /><br /> CAPTAIN CAT<br /><br />Rosie Probert.<br /><br /> ROSIE PROBERT<br /><br />Remember her.<br />She is forgetting.<br />The earth which filled her mouth<br />Is vanishing from her.<br />Remember me.<br />I have forgotten you.<br />I am going into the darkness of the darkness for ever.<br />I have forgotten that I was ever born.<br /><br /> CHILD<br /><br />Look,<br /><br /> FIRST VOICE<br /><br />says a child to her mother as they pass by the window of<br />Schooner House,<br /><br /> CHILD<br /><br />Captain Cat is crying<br /><br /> FIRST VOICE<br /><br />Captain Cat is crying<br /><br /> CAPTAIN CAT<br /><br />Come back, come back,<br /><br /> FIRST VOICE<br /><br />up the silences and echoes of the passages of the eternal<br />night.<br /><br />Read the whole thing here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://gutenberg.net.au/ebooks06/0608221h.html">http://gutenberg.net.au/ebooks06/0608...</a><br /><br />And should you ever be so privileged as to find Guy Masterton's rendition at a theatre, be thoroughly ashamed of yourself if you do not crawl over broken glass to get there. The Times in 1997 said "ONE OF THE MOST INVENTIVE, REMARKABLE PERFORMANCES OF THE DECADE." It deserves to be in capital letters. I saw it in the Adelaide Fringe a few days ago, it is back in the UK over the next months.<br /><br />Listen to Guy performing part of Capt Cat's lament about Rosie here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.theatretoursinternational.com/GMMP3s/MilkWoodCapCatRosieProb.mp3">http://www.theatretoursinternational....</a><br /><br />It does speak for itself, but if you would like a review, I leave that to my betters: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18224086">http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/...</a> Trevor's done a great job.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1460177515" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1460177515" />
    <a title="Gary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45221326-gary"><img alt="Gary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601699453p2/45221326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1460177515?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary" href="/user/show/45221326-gary">Gary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780563388609" href="/book/show/360912.Under_Milk_Wood">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Dylan Thomas fans, Richard Burton fans, poetry lovers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Gary by: </span>
      Colchester Royal Grammar School, c1976
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45221326-gary?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45221326-gary?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45221326-gary?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45221326-gary?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1460177515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7060268787965041730">Under Milk Wood is exactly what it says it is - a play for voices; and no-one's voice does it more justice than that of Richard Burton, a Welshman whose reading of this work is committed, passionate, resonant, rich and second-to-none.<br/>I should also say that this is not a monologue. Burton is the narrator but there is also a full cast of actors reading all the parts, which brings the play to life and gives it depth.<br/>If you liked reading the play, listen to this and feel its power. I might try liste</span>
  <span id="freeText7060268787965041730" style="display:none">Under Milk Wood is exactly what it says it is - a play for voices; and no-one's voice does it more justice than that of Richard Burton, a Welshman whose reading of this work is committed, passionate, resonant, rich and second-to-none.<br />I should also say that this is not a monologue. Burton is the narrator but there is also a full cast of actors reading all the parts, which brings the play to life and gives it depth.<br />If you liked reading the play, listen to this and feel its power. I might try listening to it whilst reading it at the same time.<br />The audio version is also available on Spotify.<br />Wonderful stuff.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7060268787965041730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_721106129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/721106129" />
    <a title="Stuart Aken" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4176122-stuart-aken"><img alt="Stuart Aken" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595172057p2/4176122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/721106129?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stuart Aken" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stuart Aken" href="/user/show/4176122-stuart-aken">Stuart Aken</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer721106129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13762104799389090861">Many years ago, I bought the vinyl LP of the BBC radio production of Dylan Thomas’ Under Milk Wood. It’s subtitled, ‘A Play for Voices’, and that’s about as accurate a description as I can think of. The radio production is superb, with the brilliant Richard Burton articulating the First Voice in his own inimitable style. A wonderful listening experience.<br/><br/>But what of the text? I picked up a copy from a small independent bookshop whilst shopping in Beverley with my daughter for a student cook book,</span>
  <span id="freeText13762104799389090861" style="display:none">Many years ago, I bought the vinyl LP of the BBC radio production of Dylan Thomas’ Under Milk Wood. It’s subtitled, ‘A Play for Voices’, and that’s about as accurate a description as I can think of. The radio production is superb, with the brilliant Richard Burton articulating the First Voice in his own inimitable style. A wonderful listening experience.<br /><br />But what of the text? I picked up a copy from a small independent bookshop whilst shopping in Beverley with my daughter for a student cook book, which we also found.<br /><br />The text is inevitably flavoured by my memory of the broadcast. I hear the various voices, all of them Welsh, as I turn the pages. It’s a dazzling piece of writing. The characters are alive and so distinctive. The words bring to life real people, individuals drawn from Dylan’s past. He must have been a great observer of people, if his understanding of them is anything to go by. The stories they tell, the opinions they express, the incidents they cause and observe, all point to a creator who lived with them on intimate terms.<br /><br />The occasional melancholy and touch of genuine sorrow apart, the play is bursting with humour. Here is a piece that celebrates life, celebrates what it is to be a human being. It is, unescapably, very Welsh in terms of language and a view of village life, but it manages to encompass all human experience in spite of its parochial setting. I laughed out loud through much of the reading, so full of joy and exuberance is the text.<br /><br />If you want a brief interlude of fun, entertainment and wonder at the sheer genius of a man who could do amazing things with words, this is for you. This is one of those rare experiences in life: a perfectly created piece of imaginative storytelling. Brilliant. You’ll love it!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13762104799389090861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1898058365?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhys" href="/user/show/1138007-rhys">Rhys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1898058365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17390448730431866491">Believe it or not, this is the first time I have read this extraordinary play <i>properly</i>... We had to read it in school. I didn't really understand it back then, though I quite liked it. But I remembered very little of it, apart from the scene with the ghosts of Captain Cat's crewmen and the fact that one of the female characters used lipstick on her nipples (at the time I just found this inexplicable; now I find it merely eccentric). Although I dipped into the play in the ensuing years, I never r</span>
  <span id="freeText17390448730431866491" style="display:none">Believe it or not, this is the first time I have read this extraordinary play <i>properly</i>... We had to read it in school. I didn't really understand it back then, though I quite liked it. But I remembered very little of it, apart from the scene with the ghosts of Captain Cat's crewmen and the fact that one of the female characters used lipstick on her nipples (at the time I just found this inexplicable; now I find it merely eccentric). Although I dipped into the play in the ensuing years, I never read it all the way through. I saw the film, I heard a performance on the radio, but this was my first reading in which I <u>concentrated</u> on the words, or at least tried to... So what do I think now? It's a work of genius, no doubt about that. And yet... because there is no plot, no ingenious concepts at work, no narrative tension, my mind tended to wander a bit near the end. No matter. It is definitely worth reading despite the fact it was intended as an experience for the ears rather than the eyes...</span>
  <a data-text-id="17390448730431866491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1460195167" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1289391-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1215616814p2/1289391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1460195167?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1289391-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780563388609" href="/book/show/360912.Under_Milk_Wood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1289391-michael?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1460195167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13774888975687067602">This 1954 BBC recording featuring Richard Burton is a tour de force performance. Dylan Thomas had a sensitive ear for the rhythms of speech that informed his accentual verse and an imaginative approach to descriptive language that contributed both to his immense popularity during his all-too-brief life and after and to the dismissal of his work by many modern academic poets unable to see his value because of their tunnel-vision views of what modern poetry should be. To hear his words brought to </span>
  <span id="freeText13774888975687067602" style="display:none">This 1954 BBC recording featuring Richard Burton is a tour de force performance. Dylan Thomas had a sensitive ear for the rhythms of speech that informed his accentual verse and an imaginative approach to descriptive language that contributed both to his immense popularity during his all-too-brief life and after and to the dismissal of his work by many modern academic poets unable to see his value because of their tunnel-vision views of what modern poetry should be. To hear his words brought to life by Richard Burton, a fellow Welshman and a fellow roisterer, and by the other members of this talented ensemble is a rare treat indeed. Thomas was no mean performer himself, both on stage and off, but I think he would have been pleased by Burton's inspired interpretation. Thanks to Gary for the recommendation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13774888975687067602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
